<ul><li>As to nation, I belong to none. I have no protection at home, or resting-place abroad. The land of my birth welcomes me to her shores only as a slave, and spurns with contempt the idea of treating me differently. So that I am an outcast from the society of my childhood, and an outlaw in the land of my birth... In thinking of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">America</a>, I sometimes find myself admiring her bright blue <a href="/wiki/Sky" title="Sky">sky</a> — her grand old woods — her fertile fields — her beautiful rivers — her mighty lakes, and star-crowned mountains. But my rapture is soon checked, my <a href="/wiki/Joy" title="Joy">joy</a> is soon turned to mourning. When I remember that all is cursed with the infernal spirit of slaveholding, robbery and <a href="/wiki/Wrong" class="mw-redirect" title="Wrong">wrong</a>, — when I remember that with the waters of her noblest rivers, the tears of my brethren are borne to the ocean, disregarded and forgotten, and that her most fertile fields drink daily of the warm blood of my outraged sisters, I am filled with unutterable loathing.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.yale.edu/glc/archive/1091.htm">letter to William Lloyd Garrison</a> (1 January 1846)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I make no <a href="/wiki/Pretension" title="Pretension">pretension</a> to <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">patriotism</a>. So long as my <a href="/wiki/Voice" title="Voice">voice</a> can be heard on this or the other side of the Atlantic, I will hold up <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">America</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Lightning" title="Lightning">lightning</a> scorn of <a href="/wiki/Moral" class="mw-redirect" title="Moral">moral</a> indignation. In doing this, I shall feel myself discharging the duty of a true patriot; for he is a <a href="/wiki/Lover" class="mw-redirect" title="Lover">lover</a> of his <a href="/wiki/Country" class="mw-disambig" title="Country">country</a> who rebukes and does not excuse its <a href="/wiki/Sins" class="mw-redirect" title="Sins">sins</a>. It is <a href="/wiki/Righteousness" title="Righteousness">righteousness</a> that exalteth a <a href="/wiki/Nation" class="mw-redirect" title="Nation">nation</a> while sin is a reproach to any <a href="/wiki/People" class="mw-redirect" title="People">people</a>.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.teachingamericanhistory.org/library/index.asp?document=535">"Love of God, Love of Man, Love of Country"</a> (24 September 1847), Syracuse, New York.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The 4th of July is the first great fact in your nation's <a href="/wiki/History" title="History">history</a> — the very ring-bolt in the chain of your yet undeveloped <a href="/wiki/Destiny" title="Destiny">destiny</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pride" title="Pride">Pride</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">patriotism</a>, not less than <a href="/wiki/Gratitude" title="Gratitude">gratitude</a>, prompt you to celebrate and to hold it in perpetual <a href="/wiki/Remembrance" class="mw-redirect" title="Remembrance">remembrance</a>. I have said that the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a> is the ring-bolt to the chain of your nation's destiny; so, indeed, I regard it. The <a href="/wiki/Principles" title="Principles">principles</a> contained in that instrument are saving principles. Stand by those principles, be true to them on all occasions, in all places, against all foes, and at whatever cost.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/What_to_the_Slave_is_the_Fourth_of_July%3F" class="extiw" title="s:What to the Slave is the Fourth of July?"><i>What to the Slave is the Fourth of July?</i></a> (1852).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The way to abolish slavery in America is to vote such men into power as well use their powers for the abolition of slavery... The Constitution itself. Its language is 'we the people'. Not we the white people, not even we the citizens, not we the privileged class, not we the high, not we the low, but we the people. Not we the horses, sheep, and swine, and wheel-barrows, but we the people, we the human inhabitants. If Negroes are people, they are included in the benefits for which the Constitution of America was ordained and established. But how dare any man who pretends to be a friend to the Negro thus gratuitously concede away what the Negro has a right to claim under the Constitution?
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/the-constitution-of-the-united-states-is-it-pro-slavery-or-anti-slavery/">"The Constitution of the United States: Is It Pro-Slavery or Anti-Slavery?"</a> (26 March 1860), Glasgow, United Kingdom.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>My argument against the dissolution of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">the American Union</a> is this. It would place the slave system more exclusively under the control of the slave-holding states, and withdraw it from the power in the northern states which is opposed to slavery. <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> is essentially barbarous in its character. It, above all things else, dreads the presence of an advanced civilization. It flourishes best where it meets no reproving frowns, and hears no condemning voices. While in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">the Union</a> it will meet with both. Its hope of life, in the last resort, is to get out of the Union. I am, therefore, for drawing the bond of the Union more completely under the power of the free states. What they most dread, that I most desire.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/the-constitution-of-the-united-states-is-it-pro-slavery-or-anti-slavery/"><i>The Constitution of the United States: Is It Pro-Slavery or Anti-Slavery?</i></a> (26 March 1860), Glasgow, United Kingdom.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/Destiny" title="Destiny">destiny</a> of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/African_American" class="extiw" title="w:African American">colored American</a> ... is the destiny of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">America</a>.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, speech at the Emancipation League (12 February 1862), Boston.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>We deem it a settled point that the <a href="/wiki/Destiny" title="Destiny">destiny</a> of the colored man is bound up with that of the white people of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">this country</a>. … <i>We are here</i>, and here we are likely to be. To <a href="/wiki/Imagine" class="mw-redirect" title="Imagine">imagine</a> that we shall ever be eradicated is <a href="/wiki/Absurd" class="mw-redirect" title="Absurd">absurd</a> and ridiculous. We can be remodified, changed, assimilated, but never extinguished. We repeat, therefore, that we are <i>here</i>; and that this is <i>our</i> country; and the question for the philosophers and statesmen of the land ought to be, What principles should dictate the policy of the action toward us? We shall neither die out, nor be driven out; but shall go with this people, either as a testimony against them, or as an evidence in their favor throughout their generations.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, essay in <i>North Star</i> (November 1858); as quoted in <i>Faces at the Bottom of the Well: The Permanence of Racism</i> (1992) by Derrick Bell, p. 40.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Ours is a peculiar government, based upon a peculiar idea, and that idea is universal suffrage.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/what-the-black-man-wants/">"What the Black Man Wants"</a>, speech in Boston, Massachusetts (1865).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>It is thought by many, and said by some, that <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">this republic</a> has already seen its best days; that the historian may now write the story of its decline and fall. Two classes of men are just now especially afflicted with such forebodings. The first are those who are croakers by nature. The men who have a taste for funerals, and especially national funerals. They never see the bright side of anything, and probably never will. Like the raven in the lines of Edgar A. Poe, they have learned two words, and those are, 'never more'. They usually begin by telling us what we never shall see.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I am especially to speak to you of the character and mission of the United States, with special reference to the question whether we are the better or the worse for being composed of different races of men. I propose to consider first, what we are, second, what we are likely to be, and, thirdly, what we ought to be. Without undue vanity or unjust depreciation of others, we may claim to be, in many respects, the most fortunate of nations. We stand in relations to all others, as youth to age. Other nations have had their day of greatness and glory; we are yet to have our day, and that day is coming. The dawn is already upon us. It is bright and full of promise. Other nations have reached their culminating point. We are at the beginning of our ascent. They have apparently exhausted the conditions essential to their further growth and extension, while we are abundant in all the material essential to further national growth and greatness. The resources of European statesmanship are now sorely taxed to maintain their nationalities at their ancient height of greatness and power. American statesmanship, worthy of the name, is now taxing its energies to frame measures to meet the demands of constantly increasing expansion of power, responsibility and duty. Without fault or merit on either side, theirs or ours, the balance is largely in our favor. Like the grand old forests, renewed and enriched from decaying trunks once full of life and beauty, but now moss-covered, oozy and crumbling, we are destined to grow and flourish while they decline and fade.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>We have for a long time hesitated to adopt and carry out the only principle which can solve that difficulty and give peace, strength and security to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">the republic</a>, and that is the principle of absolute equality. We are a country of all extremes, ends and opposites. The most conspicuous example of composite nationality in the world. Our people defy all the ethnological and logical classifications. In races we range all the way from black to white, with intermediate shades which, as in the apocalyptic vision, no man can name or number... America is no longer an obscure and inaccessible country. Our ships are in every sea, our commerce is in every port, our language is heard all around the globe, steam and lightning have revolutionized the whole domain of human thought, changed all geographical relations, make a day of the present seem equal to a thousand years of the past, and the continent that Columbus only conjectured four centuries ago is now the center of the world.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>A liberal and brotherly welcome to all who are likely to come to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">the United States</a> is the only wise policy which <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">this nation</a> can adopt. It has been thoughtfully observed that every nation, owing to its peculiar character and composition, has a definite mission in the world. What that mission is, and what policy is best adapted to assist in its fulfillment, is the business of its people and its statesmen to know, and knowing, to make a noble use of this knowledge. I need not stop here to name or describe the missions of other or more ancient nationalities. Our seems plain and unmistakable. Our geographical position, our relation to the outside world, our fundamental principles of government, world-embracing in their scope and character, our vast resources, requiring all manner of labor to develop them, and our already existing composite population, all conspire to one grand end, and that is, to make us the perfect national illustration of the unity and dignity of the human family that the world has ever seen.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>In whatever else other nations may have been great and grand, our greatness and grandeur will be found in the faithful application of the principle of perfect civil equality to the people of all races and of all creeds. We are not only bound to this position by our organic structure and by our revolutionary antecedents, but by the genius of our people. Gathered here from all quarters of the globe, by a common aspiration for national liberty as against caste, divine right govern and privileged classes, it would be unwise to be found fighting against ourselves and among ourselves, it would be unadvised to attempt to set up any one race above another, or one religion above another, or prescribe any on account of race, color or creed.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>All great qualities are never found in any one man or in any one race. The whole of humanity, like the whole of everything else, is ever greater than a part. Men only know themselves by knowing others, and contact is essential to this knowledge. In one race we perceive the predominance of imagination; in another, like the Chinese, we remark its almost total absence. In one people we have the reasoning faculty; in another the genius for music; in another exists courage, in another great physical vigor, and so on through the whole list of human qualities. All are needed to temper, modify, round and complete the whole man and the whole nation. Not the least among the arguments whose consideration should dispose us to welcome among us the peoples of all countries, nationalities and colors, is the fact that all races and varieties of men are improvable. This is the grand distinguishing attribute of humanity, and separates man from all other animals. If it could be shown that any particular race of men are literally incapable of improvement, we might hesitate to welcome them here. But no such men are any where to be found, and if they were, it is not likely that they would ever trouble us with their presence. The fact that the Chinese and other nations desire to come and do come is a proof of their capacity for improvement and of their fitness to come.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>When the architect intends a grand structure, he makes the foundation broad and strong. We should imitate this prudence in laying the foundations of the future republic. There is a law of harmony in all departments of nature. The oak is in the acorn. The career and destiny of individual men are enfolded in the elements of which they are composed. The same is true of a nation. It will be something or it will be nothing. It will be great, or it will be small, according to its own essential qualities. As these are rich and varied, or pure and simple, slender and feeble, broad and strong, so will be the life and destiny of the nation itself. The stream cannot rise higher than its source. The ship cannot sail faster than the wind. The flight of the arrow depends upon the strength and elasticity of the bow, and as with these, so with a nation.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Reach a degree of civilization higher and grander than any yet attained; we should welcome to our ample continent all the nations, kindreds, tongues and peoples, and as fast as they learn our language and comprehend the duties of citizenship, we should incorporate them into the American body politic. The outspread wings of the American eagle are broad enough to shelter all who are likely to come. As a matter of selfish policy, leaving right and humanity out of the question, we cannot wisely pursue any other course. Other governments mainly depend for security upon the sword; ours depends mainly upon the friendship of the people. In all matters, in time of peace, in time of war, and at all times, it makes its appeal to the people, and to all classes of the people. Its strength lies in their friendship and cheerful support in every time of need, and that policy is a mad one which would reduce the number of its friends by excluding those who would come, or by alienating those who are already here.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">Our republic</a> is itself a strong argument in favor of composite nationality. It is no disparagement to the Americans of English descent to affirm that much of the wealth, leisure, culture, refinement and civilization of the country are due to the arm of the negro and the muscle of the Irishman. Without these, and the wealth created by their sturdy toil, English civilization had still lingered this side of the Alleghanies, and the wolf still be howling on their summits. To no class of our population are we more indebted for valuable qualities of head, heart, and hand, than to the German. Say what we will of their lager, their smoke, and their metaphysics, they have brought to us a fresh, vigorous and child-like nature; a boundless facility in the acquisition of knowledge; a subtle and far-reaching intellect, and a fearless love of truth. Though remarkable for patient and laborious thought, the true German is a joyous child of freedom, fond of manly sports, a lover of music, and a happy man generally. Though he never forgets that he is a German, he never fails to remember that he is an American.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">We</a> shall spread the network of our science and our civilization over all who seek their shelter, whether from Asia, Africa, or the isles of the sea. We shall mold them all, each after his kind, into Americans. Indian and Celt, Negro and Saxon, Latin and Teuton, Mongolian and Caucasian, Jew and gentile, all shall here bow to the same law, speak the same language, support the same government, enjoy the same liberty, vibrate with the same national enthusiasm, and seek the same national ends.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/our-composite-nationality/"><i>Our Composite Nationality</i></a> (7 December 1869), Boston, Massachusetts.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>We are not here to applaud manly courage, save as it has been displayed in a noble cause. We must never forget that victory to the rebellion meant death to the republic. We must never forget that the loyal soldiers who rest beneath this sod flung themselves between the nation and <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" class="extiw" title="w:Confederate States of America">the nation destroyers</a>. If today we have a country not boiling in an agony of blood, like <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a>, if now we have a united country, no longer cursed by <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">the hell-black system of human bondage</a>, if the American name is no longer a by-word and a hissing to a mocking earth, if the star-spangled banner floats only over free American citizens in every quarter of the land, and our country has before it a long and glorious career of justice, liberty, and civilization, we are indebted to the unselfish devotion of the noble army who rest in these honored graves all around us.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://deadconfederates.com/2015/05/25/frederick-douglass-on-decoration-day-1871-5/">"The Unknown Loyal Dead"</a> (30 May 1871), Arlington National Cemetery, Arlington County, Virginia.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>That we are here in peace today is a compliment and a credit to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">American civilization</a>, and a prophecy of still greater national enlightenment and progress in the future. I refer to the past not in malice, for this is no day for malice, but simply to place more distinctly in front the gratifying and glorious change which has come both to our white fellow citizens and ourselves, and to congratulate all upon the contrast between now and then, the new dispensation of freedom with its thousand blessings to both races, and the old dispensation of slavery with its ten thousand evils to both races, white and black. In view, then, of the past, the present, and the future, with the long and dark history of our bondage behind us, and with liberty, progress, and enlightenment before us, I again congratulate you upon this auspicious day and hour.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/oration-in-memory-of-abraham-lincoln/"><i>Oratory in Memory of Abraham Lincoln</i></a> (14 April 1876), Lincoln Park, Washington, D.C.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Social equality does not necessarily follow from civil equality, and yet for the purpose of a hell black and damning prejudice, our papers still insist that the Civil Rights Bill is a Bill to establish social equality. If it is a Bill for social equality, so is the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Declaration_of_Independence" title="United States Declaration of Independence">Declaration of Independence</a>, which declares that all men have equal rights; so is the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Sermon_on_the_Mount" class="extiw" title="w:Sermon on the Mount">Sermon on the Mount</a>, so is the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Golden_Rule" class="extiw" title="w:Golden Rule">Golden Rule</a>, that commands us to do to others as we would that others should do to us; so is the Apostolic teaching, that of one blood <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a> has made all nations to dwell on all the face of the earth; so is the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Constitution" title="United States Constitution">Constitution of the United States</a>, and so are the laws and customs of every civilized country in the world; for nowhere, outside of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">United States</a> is any man denied civil rights on account of his color.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, speech at the Civil Rights Mass-Meeting Held at Lincoln Hall (22 October 1883), as quoted in <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/lifetimesoffrede1881doug/lifetimesoffrede1881doug_djvu.txt">The Life and Times of Frederick Douglass</a></i> (1881)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Varieties of the human family appear and disappear, but humanity remains and will remain forever. The American people will one day be truer to this idea.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://teachingamericanhistory.org/library/document/the-future-of-the-colored-race/">"The Future of the Colored Race"</a> (May 1886)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>From the first I saw no chance of bettering the condition of the freedman until he should cease to be merely a freedman and should become a citizen. I insisted that there was no safety for him or for anybody else in America outside the American government; that to guard, protect, and maintain his liberty the freedman should have the ballot; that the liberties of the American people were dependent upon the ballot-box, the jury-box, and the cartridge-box; that without these no class of people could live and flourish in this country; and this was now the word for the hour with me, and the word to which the people of the North willingly listened when I spoke. Hence, regarding as I did the elective franchise as the one great power by which all civil rights are obtained, enjoyed, and maintained under our form of government, and the one without which freedom to any class is delusive if not impossible, I set myself to work with whatever force and energy I possessed to secure this power for the recently-emancipated millions.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Frederick_Douglass" title="Frederick Douglass">Frederick Douglass</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://docsouth.unc.edu/neh/dougl92/dougl92.html"><i>The Life and Times of Frederick Douglass</i></a> (1892), p. 460</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="E">E</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: E">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:K._West.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/K._West.jpg/220px-K._West.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/K._West.jpg/330px-K._West.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/72/K._West.jpg/440px-K._West.jpg 2x" data-file-width="750" data-file-height="502" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:K._West.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Too many of us look upon Americans as dollar chasers. This is a cruel libel, even if it is reiterated thoughtlessly by the Americans themselves. ~ <a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Naturalization_ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Naturalization_ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg/220px-Naturalization_ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Naturalization_ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg/330px-Naturalization_ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e1/Naturalization_ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg/440px-Naturalization_ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1928" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Naturalization_ceremony_at_Kennedy_Space_Center.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>We are, proudly, a people with no sense of class or caste. We judge no man by his name or inheritance, but by what he does, and for what he stands. And so likewise do we judge other nations. The right of no nation depends upon the date of its birth or the size of its power. ~ <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC-09611.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/USMC-09611.jpg/220px-USMC-09611.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/USMC-09611.jpg/330px-USMC-09611.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/USMC-09611.jpg/440px-USMC-09611.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1126" data-file-height="854" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:USMC-09611.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>I believe that the United States as a government, if it is going to be true to its own founding documents, does have the job of working toward that time when there is no discrimination made on such inconsequential reason as race, color, or religion. ~ <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Monticello_Naturalization_Ceremony.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Monticello_Naturalization_Ceremony.jpg/220px-Monticello_Naturalization_Ceremony.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Monticello_Naturalization_Ceremony.jpg/330px-Monticello_Naturalization_Ceremony.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/24/Monticello_Naturalization_Ceremony.jpg/440px-Monticello_Naturalization_Ceremony.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Monticello_Naturalization_Ceremony.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">We</a> are a people born of many peoples. Our culture, our skills, our very aspirations have been shaped by immigrants, and their sons and daughters, from all the Earth. ~ <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight D. Eisenhower</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush-Mbeki.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bush-Mbeki.jpg/220px-Bush-Mbeki.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bush-Mbeki.jpg/330px-Bush-Mbeki.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/23/Bush-Mbeki.jpg/440px-Bush-Mbeki.jpg 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="342" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bush-Mbeki.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>As there can be no second class citizens before the law of America, so, we believe, there can be no second-class nations before the law of the world community. ~ <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Nch_children_parade.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Nch_children_parade.jpg/220px-Nch_children_parade.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="364" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ae/Nch_children_parade.jpg/330px-Nch_children_parade.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/a/ae/Nch_children_parade.jpg 2x" data-file-width="387" data-file-height="640" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Nch_children_parade.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The proudest human that walks the earth is a free American citizen. ~ <a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_United_States_Women%27s_Soccer_Team_Ticker-Tape_Parade_New_York_City_(19585111425).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_United_States_Women%27s_Soccer_Team_Ticker-Tape_Parade_New_York_City_%2819585111425%29.jpg/220px-The_United_States_Women%27s_Soccer_Team_Ticker-Tape_Parade_New_York_City_%2819585111425%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_United_States_Women%27s_Soccer_Team_Ticker-Tape_Parade_New_York_City_%2819585111425%29.jpg/330px-The_United_States_Women%27s_Soccer_Team_Ticker-Tape_Parade_New_York_City_%2819585111425%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/The_United_States_Women%27s_Soccer_Team_Ticker-Tape_Parade_New_York_City_%2819585111425%29.jpg/440px-The_United_States_Women%27s_Soccer_Team_Ticker-Tape_Parade_New_York_City_%2819585111425%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5616" data-file-height="3744" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_United_States_Women%27s_Soccer_Team_Ticker-Tape_Parade_New_York_City_(19585111425).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>America is the land of opportunity. It certainly was for <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jill_Ellis" class="extiw" title="w:Jill Ellis">me</a>. ~ <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jill_Ellis" class="extiw" title="w:Jill Ellis">Jill Ellis</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> and America clash so often not because they are so irreconcilably different, but because they are so alike.
<ul><li><i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Economist" class="extiw" title="w:The Economist">The Economist</a></i>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.economist.com/node/5323762">"Spot the difference"</a> (20 December 2005).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>There is enormous elasticity in the American political system... The country has the capacity to deal with what it now faces, both inside and outside its borders.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_B._Edsall" class="extiw" title="w:Thomas B. Edsall">Thomas Edsall</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://opinionator.blogs.nytimes.com/2013/02/27/how-much-does-race-still-matter/?_r=0">"How Much Does Race Still Matter?"</a> (27 February 2013), <i>The Washington Post</i>, Washington, D.C.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>In America, more than anywhere else, the individual is lost in the achievements of the many. America is beginning to be the world leader in scientific investigation. American scholarship is both patient and inspiring. The Americans show an unselfish devotion to science, which is the very opposite of the conventional European view of your countrymen. Too many of us look upon Americans as dollar chasers. This is a cruel libel, even if it is reiterated thoughtlessly by the Americans themselves. It is not true that the dollar is an American fetish. The American student is not interested in dollars, not even in success as such, but in his task, the object of the search. It is his painstaking application to the study of the infinitely little and the infinitely large which accounts for his success in astronomy.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Albert_Einstein" title="Albert Einstein">Albert Einstein</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.saturdayeveningpost.com/wp-content/uploads/satevepost/what_life_means_to_einstein.pdf"><i>What Life Means to Einstein: An Interview by George Sylvester Viereck"</i></a><i>, </i>The Saturday Evening Post<i> (26 October 1929)</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The proudest human that walks the earth is a free American citizen.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eisenhower.archives.gov/education/bsa/citizenship_merit_badge/eisenhower_citizenship_quotations.pdf">talk at the Commercial Club of Chicago</a> (21 May 1948).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Let us never forget that the deep things that are American are the soul and the spirit. The Statue of Liberty is not tired, and not because it is made of bronze. It is because no matter what happens, here the individual is dignified because he is created in the image of his god. Let us not forget it.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eisenhower.archives.gov/education/bsa/citizenship_merit_badge/speeches/bnai_brith_dinner.pdf">remarks to the B'nai B'rith</a> (23 November 1953), Mayflower Hotel, Washington, D.C.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The eyes of the world are fixed upon us, and we must ask ourselves, what kind of an example of freedom do we give to our age? What are the true marks of our America, and what do they mean to the world?
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eisenhower.archives.gov/education/bsa/citizenship_merit_badge/speeches/address_convention_hall.pdf">address at the Philadelphia Convention Hall</a> (1 November 1956).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>We are a people born of many peoples. Our culture, our skills, our very aspirations have been shaped by immigrants, and their sons and daughters, from all the Earth. Sam Gompers from England, Andrew Carnegie from Scotland, Albert Einstein from Germany, and Booker T. Washington and Al Smith, Marconi and Caruso. Men of all nations and races and estates, they have made us what we are... So it is that the laws most binding us as a people are laws of the spirit, proclaimed in church and synagogue and mosque. These are the laws that truly declare the eternal equality of all men, of all races, before the man-made laws of our land. And we are profoundly aware that, in the world, we can claim the trust of hundreds of millions of people, across Africa and Asia, only as we ourselves hold high the banner of justice for all... We are, proudly, a people with no sense of class or caste. We judge no man by his name or inheritance, but by what he does, and for what he stands. And so likewise do we judge other nations. The right of no nation depends upon the date of its birth or the size of its power. As there can be no second class citizens before the law of America, so, we believe, there can be no second-class nations before the law of the world community.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eisenhower.archives.gov/education/bsa/citizenship_merit_badge/speeches/address_convention_hall.pdf">address at the Philadelphia Convention Hall</a> (1 November 1956).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>A foundation of our American way of life is our national respect for law.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eisenhower.archives.gov/education/bsa/citizenship_merit_badge/speeches/address_convention_hall.pdf">address to the American People on the Situation in Little Rock</a> (24 September 1957).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I believe that the United States as a government, if it is going to be true to its own founding documents, does have the job of working toward that time when there is no discrimination made on such inconsequential reason as race, color, or religion.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.eisenhower.archives.gov/all_about_ike/quotes.html#civilrights">presidential news conference</a> (13 May 1959).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Un-American activity cannot be prevented or routed out by employing un-American methods; to preserve freedom we must use the tools that freedom provides.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, as quoted in <i>The White House Years: Mandate for Change: 1953–1956: A Personal Account</i> (1963), p. 331.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I was against <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" class="extiw" title="w:Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">it</a> on two counts. First, the <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japanese</a> were ready to surrender, and it wasn't necessary to hit them with that awful thing. Second, I hated to see <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">our country</a> be the first <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Atomic_bombings_of_Hiroshima_and_Nagasaki" class="extiw" title="w:Atomic bombings of Hiroshima and Nagasaki">to use such a weapon</a>.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Dwight_D._Eisenhower" title="Dwight D. Eisenhower">Dwight Eisenhower</a>, On his stated opposition to the use of the atomic bomb against the Japanese at the end of World War II, as quoted in Newsweek (11 November 1963).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>You were kind of an outlier if you even liked football and you were a girl in <a href="/wiki/England" title="England">England</a>. So to come over here and have that opportunity? I've always said America is the land of opportunity. It certainly was for me.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jill_Ellis" class="extiw" title="w:Jill Ellis">Jillian Ellis</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.latimes.com/sports/la-sp-0602-world-cup-jill-ellis-20150602-story.html">"U.S. Coach Jill Ellis' choices put her on the path to Women's World Cup"</a> (1 June 2015), by Kevin Baxter, <i>The Los Angeles Times</i>, California.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America has been named as the world’s most generous nation in the world, where its citizens give the most to charity.
<ul><li>Loulla-Mae Eleftheriou-Smith, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.independent.co.uk/news/world/americas/america-new-zealand-and-canada-top-list-of-world-s-most-generous-nations-a6849221.html">"America, New Zealand and Canada top list of world’s most generous nations"</a> (2 February 2016), <i>Independent</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Don't they know if tomorrow a slave ship arrived at Elmina to carry us to America, so many Ghanaians would climb on board that this ship would sink to the bed of the ocean from our weight?
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elolo" class="extiw" title="w:Elolo">Elolo</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=vnnGAgAAQBAJ&amp;printsec=frontcover"><i>Searching for Zion, The Quest for Home in the African Diaspora</i></a> (2013), by Emily Raboteau, Atlantic Monthly Press, p. 223.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I live in America, I feel such a debt to America. I love America, with all my heart.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Michael_Enright_(actor)" class="extiw" title="w:Michael Enright (actor)">Michael Enright</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/blogs/worldviews/wp/2015/06/01/why-this-hollywood-actor-dropped-everything-to-fight-the-islamic-state-in-syria/">"Why this Hollywood actor dropped everything to fight the Islamic State in Syria"</a> (1 June 2015), by Abby Phillip, <i>The Washington Post</i>.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="F">F</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: F">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_1856-71_George_Caleb_Bingham.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_1856-71_George_Caleb_Bingham.jpg/220px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_1856-71_George_Caleb_Bingham.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_1856-71_George_Caleb_Bingham.jpg/330px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_1856-71_George_Caleb_Bingham.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6b/Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_1856-71_George_Caleb_Bingham.jpg/440px-Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_1856-71_George_Caleb_Bingham.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1793" data-file-height="1125" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Washington_Crossing_the_Delaware_1856-71_George_Caleb_Bingham.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Mankind are all formed by the same almighty being, alike objects of his care and equally designed for the enjoyment of happiness... The political creed of America fully coincides with the position. ~ <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flags_of_the_United_States_and_France_(Boston_Public_Library).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flags_of_the_United_States_and_France_%28Boston_Public_Library%29.jpg/220px-Flags_of_the_United_States_and_France_%28Boston_Public_Library%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="283" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flags_of_the_United_States_and_France_%28Boston_Public_Library%29.jpg/330px-Flags_of_the_United_States_and_France_%28Boston_Public_Library%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/50/Flags_of_the_United_States_and_France_%28Boston_Public_Library%29.jpg/440px-Flags_of_the_United_States_and_France_%28Boston_Public_Library%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="932" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flags_of_the_United_States_and_France_(Boston_Public_Library).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>It seems to me that the United States and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> can learn from each other. French universalism, or its equivalent, is a powerful weapon against racism, which is based on the belief in innate unalterable differences among human groups. Stressing what rights all people have because of what they have in common remains at the heart of anti-racism. ~ <a href="/wiki/George_M._Fredrickson" title="George M. Fredrickson">George M. Fredrickson</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li>Rally round the flag, boys—<br />Give it to the breeze!<br />That's the banner that we bore<br />On the land and seas.<br />Brave hearts are under it,<br />Let the traitors brag,<br />Gallant lads, fire away!<br />And fight for the flag.<br />Their flag is but a rag—<br />Ours is the true one;<br />Up with the Stars and Stripes!<br /> with the new one!<br />Let our colors fly, boys—<br />Guard them day and night;<br />For victory is liberty,<br />And God will bless the right.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/James_Thomas_Fields" title="James Thomas Fields">James Thomas Fields</a>, "The Stars and Stripes"; reported in Florence Adams and Elizabeth McCarrick, <i>Highdays &amp; Holidays</i> (1927), pp. 182–83.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Democracy is the creed of a province; it dwells in fetid wards. Republicanism is the religion of a nation; it creates imperial commonwealths out of desert wastes. These 'imperial commonwealths' constitute the foremost nation of the earth. The American republic. It leads them all in public school systems, home comforts, multiplicity of labor-saving machinery, public service, perfect autonomy of government for local communities, modes of travel, engines of general intelligence, public caravansaries, means of adjudicating disputes between man and man, freedom of thought, religion, press and speech, and in the utmost freedom of action in individuals consistent with good order and the rights of others, without the slightest government restraint or espionage. Notwithstanding the crimes of the south against the blacks, we hold the beacon of civil liberty and personal equality higher than any other nation. The light of our civilization goes farther into the jungles of ignorance and barbarism, deeper into the dungeons of tyranny and oppression than that of any other people. Nations, the guiding star of the world. We are the load-stone of nations, the guiding star of the world.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Frank_Abial_Flower" class="extiw" title="w:Frank Abial Flower">Frank Abial Flower</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=VmkFAAAAQAAJ&amp;pg=PA449&amp;lpg=PA449&amp;dq=print+matthews+1883+copiah&amp;hl=en#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false"><i>History of the Republican Party: Embracing Its Origin, Growth and Mission</i></a> (1 July 1884), by F.A. Flower, Grand Rapids, Michigan: Union Book Company, p. 10.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Equal rights belonged to all Americans regardless of race.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Foner" class="extiw" title="w:Eric Foner">Eric Foner</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=cwVkgrvctCcC&amp;printsec=frontcover&amp;dq=%22Eric+Foner%22+%22Republicans%22&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0ahUKEwiOwdup3aLLAhVK7SYKHZufDmUQ6AEIRjAH#v=onepage&amp;q=%22Eric%20Foner%22%20%22Republicans%22&amp;f=false"><i>Reconstruction: America's Unfinished Revolution, 1863-1877</i></a>, p. xxiv</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Many things claimed as uniquely American, a devotion to individual freedom, for example, or social opportunity, exist in other countries. But birthright citizenship does make the United States unique in the developed world. No European nation recognizes the principle.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Eric_Foner" class="extiw" title="w:Eric Foner">Eric Foner</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.is/NFGmx#selection-2523.0-2523.383">"What is an American?: Birthright citizenship, more than anything else, makes our country exceptional"</a> (6 September 2015), by E. Foner, <i>Pittsburgh Post-Gazette</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Let us put an end to self-inflicted wounds. Let us remember that our national unity is a most priceless asset.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerald R. Ford">Gerald Ford</a>, as quoted in address to joint session of the United States Congress (10 April 1975).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>February 19 is the anniversary of a very, very sad day in American history. It was on that date in 1942 that Executive Order 9066 was issued resulting in the uprooting of many, many loyal Americans. Over 100,000 persons of Japanese ancestry were removed from their homes, detained in special camps, and eventually relocated. We now know what we should have known then. Not only was that evacuation wrong but Japanese-Americans were and are loyal Americans. On the battlefield and at home the names of Japanese-Americans have been and continue to be written in history for the sacrifices and the contributions they have made to the well-being and to the security of this, our common Nation. Executive Order 9066 ceased to be effective at the end of World War II. Because there was no formal statement of its termination, there remains some concern among Japanese-Americans that there yet may be some life in that obsolete document. The proclamation that I am signing here today should remove all doubt on that matter. I call upon the American people to affirm with me the unhyphenated American promise that we have learned from the tragedy of that long ago experience; forever to treasure liberty and justice for each individual American and resolve that this kind of error shall never be made again.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Gerald_R._Ford" class="mw-redirect" title="Gerald R. Ford">Gerald Ford</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.fordlibrarymuseum.gov/library/speeches/760111p.htm"><i>President Gerald R. Ford's Proclamation 4417, Confirming the Termination of the Executive Order Authorizing Japanese-American Internment During World War II</i></a> (19 February 1976).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America continues to be, for many, a land of dreams. Dreams which lead to action, to participation, to commitment. Dreams which awaken what is deepest and truest in the life of a people. In recent centuries, millions of people came to this land to pursue their dream of building a future in freedom. We, the people of this continent, are not fearful of foreigners, because most of us were once foreigners. I say this to you as the son of immigrants, knowing that so many of you are also descended from immigrants... Tragically, the rights of those who were here long before us were not always respected. For those peoples and their nations, from the heart of American democracy, I wish to reaffirm my highest esteem and appreciation. Those first contacts were often turbulent and violent, but it is difficult to judge the past by the criteria of the present. Nonetheless, when the stranger in our midst appeals to us, we must not repeat the sins and the errors of the past. We must resolve now to live as nobly and as justly as possible, as we educate new generations not to turn their back on our 'neighbors' and everything around us.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Pope_Francis" title="Pope Francis">Pope Francis</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.c-span.org/video/?328063-1/pope-francis-address-joint-meeting-congress">Pope Francis Address to Joint Meeting of Congress</a> (24 September 2015). As quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.washingtonpost.com/local/social-issues/transcript-pope-franciss-speech-to-congress/2015/09/24/6d7d7ac8-62bf-11e5-8e9e-dce8a2a2a679_story.html">"Transcript: Pope Francis' Speech to Congress"</a> (24 September 2015), <i>The Washington Post</i>.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>[M]ankind are all formed by the same Almighty being, alike objects of his Care &amp; equally designed for the Enjoyment of Happiness the Christian Religion teaches us to believe &amp; the Political Creed of America fully coincides with the Position... [B]lessings ought rightfully to be administered, without distinction of Colour, to all descriptions of People, so they indulge themselves in the pleasing expectation, that nothing, which can be done for the relive of the unhappy objects of their care, will be either omitted or delayed... From a persuasion that equal liberty was originally the Portion, It is still the Birthright of all men.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Franklin" title="Benjamin Franklin">Benjamin Franklin</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20060521035446/http://www.ushistory.org:80/documents/antislavery.htm">"Petition from the Pennsylvania Society for the Abolition of Slavery"</a> (3 February 1790)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>It seems to me that the United States and <a href="/wiki/France" title="France">France</a> can learn from each other. French universalism, or its equivalent, is a powerful weapon against racism, which is based on the belief in innate unalterable differences among human groups. Stressing what rights all people have because of what they have in common remains at the heart of anti-racism. A stronger awareness of such human commonality may be needed in the United States at a time when a stress on diversity and ethnic particularism may deprive us of any compelling vision of the larger national community and impede cooperation in the pursuit of a free and just society. On the other hand the identification of such universalism with a particular national identity and with specific cultural traits that go beyond essential human rights can lead to an intolerance of the <i>Other</i> that approaches color-coded racism in its harmful effects.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/George_M._Fredrickson" title="George M. Fredrickson">George M. Fredrickson</a>, <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20031208020244/http://www.yale.edu/glc/events/race/Fredrickson.pdf">Race, Ethnicity, and National Identity in France and the United States: A Comparative Historical Overview</a></i>, (8 November 2003).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The United States is arguably the world's oldest democracy. Its people benefit from a vibrant electoral system, a strong rule-of-law tradition, robust freedoms of expression and religious belief, and a wide array of other civil liberties. The United States remains a major destination point for immigrants and has largely been successful in integrating newcomers from all backgrounds.
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://freedomhouse.org/report/freedom-world/2017/united-states"><i>Freedom House</i></a></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>In the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">United States</a>, minority populations were never an indigestible mass—with the major exceptions of the one ethnic group that did not come here voluntarily (African Americans) and those who were here when Europeans arrived (American Indians). The rest all came, clustered and dispersed, and added new cultural layers to the general society. <b><a href="/wiki/Immigration" title="Immigration">This</a> has always been the strength of the <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">United States</a></b>.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/George_Friedman" title="George Friedman">George Friedman</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20170628085246/http://www.mysearch.org.uk/website1/pdf/715.2.pdf"><i>The Next 100 Years: A Forecast for the 21st Century</i></a> (2009), New York: Doubleday, pp. 224&#8211;225</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The United States' model is a little bit more liberal and therefore we do less redistribution.
<ul><li>Francis Fukuyama, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.rferl.org/content/fukuyama-putinism-islamic-state-liberal-democracy/27518924.html">"Fukuyama: 'Putinism', Radical Islam No Alternative To Liberal Democracy"</a> (30 January 2016), by *Charles Recknagel, <i>Radio Free Europe: Radio Liberty</i>.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>There are two Americas. One is the America of <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Lincoln</a> and <a href="/wiki/Adlai_Stevenson" class="mw-redirect" title="Adlai Stevenson">Adlai Stevenson</a>; the other is the America of <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Roosevelt" title="Theodore Roosevelt">Teddy Roosevelt</a> and the modern <a href="/wiki/Patriotism" title="Patriotism">superpatriots</a>. One is generous and humane, the other narrowly egotistical; one is self-critical, the other self-righteous; one is sensible, the other romantic; one is good-humored, the other solemn; one is inquiring, the other pontificating; one is moderate, the other filled with passionate intensity; one is judicious and the other arrogant in the use of great power.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/J._William_Fulbright" class="extiw" title="w:J. William Fulbright">J. William Fulbright</a>, <i>The Arrogance of Power</i> (1966).</li></ul></li></ul>

</p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Scene_at_the_Signing_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_States.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Scene_at_the_Signing_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_States.jpg/220px-Scene_at_the_Signing_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_States.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="142" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Scene_at_the_Signing_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_States.jpg/330px-Scene_at_the_Signing_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_States.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9d/Scene_at_the_Signing_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_States.jpg/440px-Scene_at_the_Signing_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_States.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="1933" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Scene_at_the_Signing_of_the_Constitution_of_the_United_States.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>To grant suffrage to the black man in <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">this country</a> is not innovation, but restoration. It is a return to the ancient principles and practices of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States" class="extiw" title="w:Founding Fathers of the United States">the fathers</a>. ~ <a href="/wiki/James_A._Garfield" title="James A. Garfield">James A. Garfield</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:B-2_Spirit_original.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/B-2_Spirit_original.jpg/220px-B-2_Spirit_original.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="138" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/B-2_Spirit_original.jpg/330px-B-2_Spirit_original.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/B-2_Spirit_original.jpg/440px-B-2_Spirit_original.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1252" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:B-2_Spirit_original.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The essence of U.S. military predominance in the world is, ultimately, the fact that it can, at will, drop bombs, with only a few hours' notice, at absolutely any point on the surface of the planet. No other government has ever had anything remotely like this sort of capability. ~ <a href="/wiki/David_Graeber" title="David Graeber">David Graeber</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Capitol_dome_Jan_2006.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/US_Capitol_dome_Jan_2006.jpg/220px-US_Capitol_dome_Jan_2006.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/US_Capitol_dome_Jan_2006.jpg/330px-US_Capitol_dome_Jan_2006.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5a/US_Capitol_dome_Jan_2006.jpg/440px-US_Capitol_dome_Jan_2006.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6831" data-file-height="7614" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:US_Capitol_dome_Jan_2006.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Leave the matter of religion to the family altar, the church, and the private school, supported entirely by private contributions. Keep the church and the state forever separate. ~ <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S. Grant">Ulysses S. Grant</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States_(1867%E2%80%931877).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281867%E2%80%931877%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281867%E2%80%931877%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281867%E2%80%931877%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281867%E2%80%931877%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f3/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281867%E2%80%931877%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281867%E2%80%931877%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1781" data-file-height="937" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States_(1867%E2%80%931877).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Protect the law-abiding citizen, whether of native or foreign birth, wherever his rights are jeopardized or the flag of our country floats. ~ <a href="/wiki/Ulysses_S._Grant" title="Ulysses S.
