<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elijah_Muhammad_NYWTS-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Elijah_Muhammad_NYWTS-2.jpg/220px-Elijah_Muhammad_NYWTS-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="236" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Elijah_Muhammad_NYWTS-2.jpg/330px-Elijah_Muhammad_NYWTS-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d2/Elijah_Muhammad_NYWTS-2.jpg/440px-Elijah_Muhammad_NYWTS-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1515" data-file-height="1627" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elijah_Muhammad_NYWTS-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>America represents herself as a Christian nation. ... They profess to be a friend and defenders of all peace-loving and freedom-loving people. The only people we really see that they want to be friends of are themselves and their kind. They are really sincere when they say that they are freedom-loving people. Above all, the White man the world over wants to be free to rule and dominate the aboriginal people. ~ <a href="/wiki/Elijah_Muhammad" title="Elijah Muhammad">Elijah Muhammad</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li>Americans never quit.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">Douglas MacArthur</a>, as president of the U.S. Olympic committee when the manager of the U.S. boxing team in the 1928 Olympic games wanted to withdraw the team because of what he thought was an unfair decision against an American boxer; reported in <i>The New York Times</i> (9 August 1928), p. 13</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America has evolved a model for this new free world... America has demonstrated that peoples of the East and peoples of the West may walk side by side in mutual respect and with mutual benefit.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Douglas_MacArthur" title="Douglas MacArthur">Douglas MacArthur</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://ussmissouri.org/learn-the-history/surrender/general-macarthurs-radio-address/">radio address</a> (2 September 1945).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The highest number to which, according to the best computation, a <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/standing_army" class="extiw" title="w:standing army">standing army</a> can be carried in any country, does not exceed one hundredth part of the whole number of souls; or one twenty-fifth part of the number able to bear arms. This proportion would not yield, in the United States, an army of more than twenty-five or thirty thousand men. To these would be opposed a militia amounting to near half a million of citizens with arms in their hands, officered by men chosen from among themselves, fighting for the common liberties and united and conducted by governments possessing their affections and confidence. It may well be doubted whether a militia thus circumstanced could ever be conquered by such a proportion of regular troops. Those who are best acquainted with the late successful resistance of this country against the British arms will be most inclined to deny the possibility of it. Besides the advantage of being armed, which the Americans possess over the people of almost every other nation, the existence of subordinate governments, to which the people are attached and by which the militia officers are appointed, forms a barrier against the enterprises of ambition, more insurmountable than any which a simple government of any form can admit of. Notwithstanding the military establishments of the several kingdoms of Europe, which are carried as far as the public resources will bear, the governments are afraid to trust the people with arms.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a>, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Federalist_No._46" class="extiw" title="w:Federalist No. 46"><i>Federalist No. 46</i></a> (1788).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The government of the United States is a definite government, confined to specified objects. It is not like the state governments, whose powers are more general. Charity is no part of the legislative duty of the government.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://memory.loc.gov/cgi-bin/query/r?ammem/hlaw:@field(DOCID+@lit(ed00423)):">Speech, House of Representatives, during the debate "On the Memorial of the Relief Committee of Baltimore, for the Relief of St. Domingo Refugees"</a> (1794).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>It is a settled policy of America, that as peace is better than war, war is better than tribute. The United States, while they wish for war with no nation, will buy peace with none.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a>, letter to Wolcott Chauncy and William Shaler, summarizing the Treaty of 1815, which ended the Second Barbary War and, with it, the practice of the U.S. government paying tribute to pirate states, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://books.google.com/books?id=YMwRAAAAYAAJ&amp;pg=PA46%7C">History and Present Condition of Tripoli:</a> With Some Accounts of the Other Barbary States" by Robert Greenhow, published by T.W. White, 1835, page 46.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The United States, having been the first to abolish within the extent of their authority the transportation of the natives of Africa into slavery, by prohibiting the introduction of slaves and by punishing their citizens participating in the traffic, cannot but be gratified at the progress made by concurrent efforts of other nations toward a general suppression of <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">so great an evil</a>.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=PsFnB7FA11YC&amp;pg=PA200&amp;dq=%22Rendered+impossible+by+the+prejudices+of+the+whites%22&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0CCMQ6AEwAWoVChMI8uuN6dbUxwIVBD0-Ch1EqwFq#v=onepage&amp;q=%22Rendered%20impossible%20by%20the%20prejudices%20of%20the%20whites%22&amp;f=false"><i>State of the Nation</i></a> (3 December 1816).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>It has been said that America is a country for the poor, not for the rich. There would be more correctness in saying it is the country for both, where the latter have a relish for free government; but, proportionally, more for the former than for the latter.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/jstor-2713830/2713830_djvu.txt">letter to F. Corbin (26 November 1820)</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.jstor.org/stable/2713830?seq=1#page_scan_tab_contents"><i>Letters and other Writings of James Madison: 1816-1828</i></a>, III, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=CDkMAAAAIAAJ&amp;pg=PA194&amp;lpg=PA194&amp;dq=%22It+has+been+said+that+America+is+a+country+for+the+poor%22&amp;source=bl&amp;ots=IhaCmIE8FV&amp;sig=NQAjX5Ue9GMcFLNji9FjLkXWaP8&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0CCkQ6AEwBGoVChMIxtjzuvXYxwIVBNg-Ch2ckg_0#v=onepage&amp;q=%22It%20has%20been%20said%20that%20America%20is%20a%20country%20for%20the%20poor%22&amp;f=false">pp. 194-195</a>.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">Slavery</a> is, as you justly complain, a sad blot on <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">our free country</a>.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/James_Madison" title="James Madison">James Madison</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=Elh0sAhIVvAC&amp;pg=PA85&amp;dq=%22SAD+BLOT+ON+OUR+FREE+COUNTRY%22&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ved=0CCkQ6AEwAmoVChMI47DWxfTQxwIVRFQ-Ch2fvwWA#v=onepage&amp;q=%22SAD%20BLOT%20ON%20OUR%20FREE%20COUNTRY%22&amp;f=false">letter to La Fayette</a> (1821).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I've never met anyone who told me they were angry at China or France or Russia for failing to help them. Where people are desperate, it is still America they count on, whether they love or scorn it, and America they blame when aid does not come. They know that the United States is the one country with both the power and predilection to stand up for them.
<ul><li>Tom Malinowski, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.theatlantic.com/international/archive/2017/03/trump-human-rights-freedom-state-department/520677/?utm_source=twb">"What America Stood For"</a> (25 March 2017), <i>The Atlantic</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I am proud that I am an American citizen of Japanese ancestry, for my very background makes me appreciate more fully the wonderful advantages of this nation. I believe in her institutions, ideals, and traditions. I glory in her heritage, I boast of her history. I trust in her future. She has granted me liberties and opportunities such as no individual enjoys in this world today. She has given me an education befitting kings. She has entrusted me with the responsibilities of the franchise. She has permitted me to build a home, to earn a livelihood, to worship, think, speak, and act as I please, as a free man equal to every other man. Although some individuals may discriminate against me, I shall never become bitter or lose faith, for I know that such persons are not representative of the majority of the American people. True, I shall do all in my power to discourage such practices, but I shall do it in the American way. Above board, in the open, through courts of law, by education, by proving myself to be worthy of equal treatment and consideration.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masaji_Masaoka" class="extiw" title="w:Masaji Masaoka">Masaji Masaoka</a>, Japanese American Citizens League (1940), as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=eWs0AQAAQBAJ&amp;printsec=frontcover&amp;dq=imperial+japanese+army+yenne&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=-tGPVYSjNYzEggSFp4DwBQ&amp;ved=0CDMQ6AEwAg#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false"><i>Rising Sons: The Japanese American GIs Who Fought for the United States</i></a>, by Bill Yenne.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I am firm in my belief that American sportsmanship and attitude of fair play will judge citizenship and patriotism on the basis of action and achievement, and not on the basis of physical characteristics. Because I believe in America, and I trust she believes in me, and because I have received innumerable benefits from her, I pledge myself to do honor to her at all times and all places, to defend her against all enemies, foreign and domestic, to actively assume my duties and obligations as a citizen, cheerfully and without any reservations whatsoever, in the hope that I may become a better American in a greater America.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Masaji_Masaoka" class="extiw" title="w:Masaji Masaoka">Masaji Masaoka</a>, Japanese American Citizens League (1940), as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://books.google.com/books?id=eWs0AQAAQBAJ&amp;printsec=frontcover&amp;dq=imperial+japanese+army+yenne&amp;hl=en&amp;sa=X&amp;ei=-tGPVYSjNYzEggSFp4DwBQ&amp;ved=0CDMQ6AEwAg#v=onepage&amp;q&amp;f=false"><i>Rising Sons: The Japanese American GIs Who Fought for the United States</i></a>, by Bill Yenne.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America stand up. We love <a href="/wiki/United_States_Armed_Forces" title="United States Armed Forces">our military</a> and we love our country but we fucking hate Trump.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Eminem" title="Eminem">Marshall B. Mathers</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://twitter.com/Eminem/status/917922469775925248">"The Storm"</a> (October 2017)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America, the only nation ever founded in the name of liberty.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cbsnews.com/stories/1998/05/29/national/main10557.shtml">"Goldwater Called 'Great Patriot'" at <i>CBS News</i> (29 May 1998)</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external autonumber" href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=FLATQAU-Hw0">[2]</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>We are Americans first, Americans last, Americans always. Let us argue our differences. But remember we are not enemies, but comrades in a war against a real enemy, and take courage from the knowledge that our military superiority is matched only by the superiority of our ideals, and our unconquerable love for them... We're Americans, and we'll never surrender. <i>They</i> will.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, <i><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.gwu.edu/~action/2004/repconv04/mccain083004sp.html">Republican National Convention</a></i> (30 August 2004).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America is the greatest force for good in the history of the world.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nationalinterest.org/Article.aspx?id=19990">Second U.S. Presidential Debate</a> (8 October 2008).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Whatever our differences, we are fellow Americans. And please believe me when I say no association has ever meant more to me than that.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://ap.google.com/article/ALeqM5hmJfimrZW3jBur_BmaFtqj7mfFgQD948JFJG5">presidential concession speech</a> (November 2008)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Through the violence, chaos and heartache of war, through deprivation and cruelty and loss, we are always Americans, and different, stronger and better than those who would destroy us.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_McCain" title="John McCain">John McCain</a>, as quoted in "Bin Laden's death and the debate over torture" (11 May 2011), <i>The Washington Post</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The U.S. Constitution also bent over backwards to avoid using the term 'slave' or 'slavery' in the document, but the pro-slavery CSA apparently didn't have a problem calling a spade a spade.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Jim_McCullough" class="extiw" title="w:Jim McCullough">Jim McCullough</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20151108133240/http://www.jjmccullough.com/CSA.htm">"The Constitution of the Confederate States of America: What was changed? And why?"</a> (July 2006)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li><b>Riley</b>: “No stealing”? Don’t you always say <a href="/wiki/Theft" title="Theft">theft</a> in <a href="/wiki/America" class="mw-redirect" title="America">America</a> is <a href="/wiki/Justified" class="mw-redirect" title="Justified">justified</a> because the whole <a href="/wiki/Country" class="mw-disambig" title="Country">country</a> is stolen <a href="/wiki/Land" title="Land">land</a>?</li></ul>
<dl><dd><b>Huey</b>: Yeah, I sure do.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Aaron_McGruder" class="extiw" title="w:Aaron McGruder">Aaron McGruder</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Boondocks_(comic_strip)" title="The Boondocks (comic strip)">The Boondocks</a></i>, (5/16/1999)</li></ul></dd></dl>
<ul><li>America is a living structure of human lives, of all the American lives that ever were and ever will be.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Richard_McKenna" title="Richard McKenna">Richard McKenna</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sand_Pebbles" class="extiw" title="w:The Sand Pebbles"> The Sand Pebbles</a></i> (1962)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The barriers of time and space vanish. All America that ever was and ever will be lives every moment...
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Richard_McKenna" title="Richard McKenna">Richard McKenna</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Sand_Pebbles" class="extiw" title="w:The Sand Pebbles"> The Sand Pebbles</a></i> (1962)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>By the time of the Gettysburg Address, in November 1863, the North was fighting for a 'new birth of freedom' to transform the Constitution written by the founding fathers, under which the United States had become the world's largest slaveholding country, into a charter of emancipation for a republic where, as the northern version of 'The Battle Cry of Freedom' put it, 'Not a man shall be a slave'.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/James_M._McPherson" class="extiw" title="w:James M. McPherson">James M. McPherson</a>, as quoted in <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Illustrated_Battle_Cry_of_Freedom" class="extiw" title="w:The Illustrated Battle Cry of Freedom">The Illustrated Battle Cry of Freedom</a></i> (2003)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The character of our enemies testifies to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">America</a>'s greatness, for those leaders who most hate us show scant regard for their own peoples' welfare.
<ul><li><a href="/w/index.php?title=James_D._Miller&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="James D. Miller (page does not exist)">James D. Miller</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20040603070702/http://www.techcentralstation.com/041404F.html">"An Empire? You ain't Seen Nothin' Yet"</a> (14 April 2004), <i>Tech Central Station</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America - a conservative country without any conservative ideology-appears now before the world a naked and arbitrary power, as, in the name of realism, its men of decision enforce their often crackpot definitions upon world reality. The second-rate mind is in command of the ponderously spoken platitude. In the liberal rhetoric, vagueness, and in the conservative mood, irrationality, are raised to principle. Public relations and the official secret, the trivializing campaign and the terrible fact clumsily accomplished, are replacing the reasoned debate of political ideas in the privately incorporated economy, the military ascendancy, and the political vacuum of modern America.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/C._Wright_Mills" title="C. Wright Mills">C. Wright Mills</a>, <i><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/The_Power_Elite" class="extiw" title="w:The Power Elite">The Power Elite</a></i> (1956).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The American <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/elite" class="extiw" title="w:elite">elite</a> does not have any real image of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/peace" class="extiw" title="w:peace">peace</a> — other than as an uneasy interlude existing precariously by virtue of the balance of mutual fright. The only seriously accepted plan for peace is the full loaded pistol.  In short, <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/war" class="extiw" title="w:war">war</a> or a high state of war-preparedness is felt to be the normal and seemingly permanent condition of the United States.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/C._Wright_Mills" title="C. Wright Mills">C. Wright Mills</a> <i>The Power Elite</i> (1956).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>In the United States ... a handful of corporations centralize decisions and responsibilities that are relevant for military and political as well as economic developments of global significance. For nowadays the military and the political cannot be separated from economic considerations of power. We now live not in an economic order or a political order, but in a political economy that is closely linked with military institutions and decisions. This is obvious in the repeated "oil crisis" in the Middle East, or in the relevance of Southeast Asia and African resources for the Western powers…
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/C._Wright_Mills" title="C. Wright Mills">C. Wright Mills</a>, <i>Character &amp; Social Structure</i> (1954).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>In America, we vote, we decide as a group of people what our policies are, and that's the way we do business. We don't let violence make those determinations for us.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Charles_A._Moose" class="mw-redirect" title="Charles A. Moose">Charles A. Moose</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.c-spanvideo.org/program/AttacksU">town hall meeting</a> (8 October 2001).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The truth is the modern <a href="/wiki/Virginia" title="Virginia">Virginians</a> departed from the teachings of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Founding_Fathers_of_the_United_States" class="extiw" title="w:Founding Fathers of the United States">the Fathers</a>.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/John_S._Mosby" title="John S. Mosby">John Singleton Mosby</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://web.archive.org/web/20131112054334/https://www.gilderlehrman.org/history-by-era/reconstruction/resources/former-confederate-officer-slavery-and-civil-war-1907">letter to Samuel "Sam" Chapman</a> (4 June 1907).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America represents herself as a Christian nation. ... They profess to be a friend and defenders of all peace-loving and freedom-loving people. The only people we really see that they want to be friends of are themselves and their kind. They are really sincere when they say that they are freedom-loving people. Above all, the White man the world over wants to be free to rule and dominate the aboriginal people.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Elijah_Muhammad" title="Elijah Muhammad">Elijah Muhammad</a>, <i>Message to the Blackman</i> (1965)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I've got nothing against any individual <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">American</a>, except that there aren't any. They're always Irish-American, African-American&#8211;there's never an American-American you can <i>blame!</i>
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Simon_Munnery" class="extiw" title="w:Simon Munnery">Simon Munnery</a>, as quoted in <i>Attention Scum</i>.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I wasn't born in America, but I got here as fast as I could.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Elon_Musk" class="extiw" title="w:Elon Musk">Elon Musk</a>, <i>Think Tank</i> interview (2008)</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="N">N</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: N">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Huey_Newton.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Huey_Newton.jpg/220px-Huey_Newton.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="222" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Huey_Newton.jpg/330px-Huey_Newton.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e5/Huey_Newton.jpg/440px-Huey_Newton.jpg 2x" data-file-width="456" data-file-height="461" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Huey_Newton.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Clear-cut superiority in things social and economic—by whatever means—has been a scruples-free premise of American ruling class authority from the society's inception to the present. The initial socioeconomic advantage, begotten by chattel slavery, was enforced by undaunted violence and the constant threat of more violence. ~ <a href="/wiki/Huey_P._Newton" title="Huey P. Newton">Huey P. Newton</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li>America will not die. As the time demands them, great men will appear, and by their combined efforts render liberty and happiness more secure. The people will be ready and answer in every emergency that may arise.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Charles_E._Nash" title="Charles E. Nash">Charles E. Nash</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://web.archive.org/web/20160528155427/http://history.house.gov/People/Detail/18846">speech to the U.S. House of Representatives</a> (7 June 1876)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America means fair play for all men.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Thomas_Nast" class="extiw" title="w:Thomas Nast">Thomas Nast</a>, <a href="/wiki/File:The_Chinese_Question_(February_1871),_by_Thomas_Nast.png" title="File:The Chinese Question (February 1871), by Thomas Nast.png">"The Chinese Question"</a> (1871), <i>Harper's Weekly</i> (18 February 1871)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Far from there being a consensus on the acceptance of slavery, sectional differences between the north and the south about the practice of it existed, and were subject of political contentions, from the beginning of the American nation!
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_Navarro" class="extiw" title="w:David Navarro">David Navarro</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://cwcrossroads.wordpress.com/2014/08/01/more-of-the-same/#comment-47695">"More of the Same"</a> (12 July 2015), <i>Crossroads</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I am certain that I speak on behalf of my entire nation when I say, today we are all Americans. In grief, as in defiance.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>, <i>Statement on the September 11 attacks</i> (20 September 2001), as quoted at the official site of <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.israelemb.org/US-Israel-Relations/US-Israel-Relations_famous.htm">Israeli embassy</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>I know what America is. America is a thing you can move very easily, move it in the right direction. They won't get in our way.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://voices.washingtonpost.com/checkpoint-washington/2010/07/netanyahu_america_is_a_thing_y.html">"Netanyahu: 'America is a thing you can move very easily'"</a> (16 July 2010), <i>The Washington Post</i>, Washington, D.C.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>If Israel has to stand alone, Israel will stand. But I know that Israel does not stand alone. I know that <i>America</i> stands with Israel.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Netanyahu" title="Benjamin Netanyahu">Benjamin Netanyahu</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.is/6C3C6">address to a joint meeting of the United States Congress</a> (3 March 2015), Washington, D.C.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Always, the rulers of an order, consistent with their own interests and solely of their own design, have employed what to them seemed to be the most optimal and efficient means of maintaining unquestioned social and economic advantage. Clear-cut superiority in things social and economic—by whatever means—has been a scruples-free premise of American ruling class authority from the society's inception to the present. The initial socioeconomic advantage, begotten by chattel slavery, was enforced by undaunted violence and the constant threat of more violence.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Huey_P._Newton" title="Huey P. Newton">Huey P. Newton</a>, <i>War Against the Panthers: A Study of Repression in America</i>, Doctoral dissertation submitted to the Faculty of <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/University_of_California_Santa_Cruz" class="extiw" title="w:University of California Santa Cruz">University of California Santa Cruz</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://archive.org/stream/WarAgainstThePanthersAStudyOfRepressionInAmerica/WATP_djvu.txt">June 1, 1980</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>At the outset of the German Government's movement against the Jews, an American visitor asked Herr <a href="/wiki/Hitler" class="mw-redirect" title="Hitler">Hitler</a> why he was making it so ruthless. The Reichskanzler replied that he had got the idea from us. Americans, he said, are the great rope and lamppost artists [i.e., lynching] of the world, known of all men as such. He was using the same methods against the Jews that we used against the loyalists of ‘76, the Indians, the Chinese on the Western coast, the Negroes, the Mexicans, the Filipinos — every helpless people in fact whom we had ever chanced to find underfoot.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Albert_Jay_Nock" class="extiw" title="w:Albert Jay Nock">Albert Jay Nock</a>, "The Jewish Problem in America," <i>Atlantic Monthly</i>, June, 1941.</li></ul></li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="O">O</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=United_States&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: O">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Navy_Hospital_Corpsman_3rd_Class_Eric_Chiarito,_left,_and_Marine_Sgt._Jonathan_Thornton_load_supplies_onto_a_forklift_at_Tacloban_Air_Base,_Philippines,_in_support_of_Operation_Damayan_Nov._14,_2013_131114-N-BX824-001.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/U.S._Navy_Hospital_Corpsman_3rd_Class_Eric_Chiarito%2C_left%2C_and_Marine_Sgt._Jonathan_Thornton_load_supplies_onto_a_forklift_at_Tacloban_Air_Base%2C_Philippines%2C_in_support_of_Operation_Damayan_Nov._14%2C_2013_131114-N-BX824-001.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/U.S._Navy_Hospital_Corpsman_3rd_Class_Eric_Chiarito%2C_left%2C_and_Marine_Sgt._Jonathan_Thornton_load_supplies_onto_a_forklift_at_Tacloban_Air_Base%2C_Philippines%2C_in_support_of_Operation_Damayan_Nov._14%2C_2013_131114-N-BX824-001.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/U.S._Navy_Hospital_Corpsman_3rd_Class_Eric_Chiarito%2C_left%2C_and_Marine_Sgt._Jonathan_Thornton_load_supplies_onto_a_forklift_at_Tacloban_Air_Base%2C_Philippines%2C_in_support_of_Operation_Damayan_Nov._14%2C_2013_131114-N-BX824-001.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="960" data-file-height="639" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:U.S._Navy_Hospital_Corpsman_3rd_Class_Eric_Chiarito,_left,_and_Marine_Sgt._Jonathan_Thornton_load_supplies_onto_a_forklift_at_Tacloban_Air_Base,_Philippines,_in_support_of_Operation_Damayan_Nov._14,_2013_131114-N-BX824-001.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>America leads; we are <i>the</i> indispensable nation. We have capacity no one else has. Our military is the best in the history of the world, and when trouble comes up anywhere in the world, they don't call Beijing. They don't call Moscow. They call us. That's the deal. ~ <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a></div></div></div>

When there's an earthquake in Haiti, take a look at who's leading the charge making sure Haiti can rebuild. That's how we roll, and that's what makes this America. ~ <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rosie_the_Riveter_(Vultee)_DS.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Rosie_the_Riveter_%28Vultee%29_DS.jpg/220px-Rosie_the_Riveter_%28Vultee%29_DS.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="176" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Rosie_the_Riveter_%28Vultee%29_DS.jpg/330px-Rosie_the_Riveter_%28Vultee%29_DS.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/Rosie_the_Riveter_%28Vultee%29_DS.jpg/440px-Rosie_the_Riveter_%28Vultee%29_DS.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4036" data-file-height="3224" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rosie_the_Riveter_(Vultee)_DS.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>What could more profoundly vindicate the idea of America than plain and humble people? Unsung, the downtrodden, the dreamers not of high station, not born to wealth or privilege, not of one religious tradition but many, coming together to shape their country's course? What greater expression of faith in the American experiment than this? ~ <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_photo_essay_120528-D-BW835-460.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Defense.gov_photo_essay_120528-D-BW835-460.jpg/220px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_120528-D-BW835-460.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Defense.gov_photo_essay_120528-D-BW835-460.jpg/330px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_120528-D-BW835-460.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d5/Defense.gov_photo_essay_120528-D-BW835-460.jpg/440px-Defense.gov_photo_essay_120528-D-BW835-460.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3654" data-file-height="2436" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Defense.gov_photo_essay_120528-D-BW835-460.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>We are an American family and we rise or fall together as one nation and as one people... We are and forever will be the United States of America... We we will continue our journey forward and remind the world just why it is that we live in the greatest nation on Earth. ~ <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_canyon_of_yellowstone.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Grand_canyon_of_yellowstone.JPG/220px-Grand_canyon_of_yellowstone.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="293" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Grand_canyon_of_yellowstone.JPG/330px-Grand_canyon_of_yellowstone.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/ed/Grand_canyon_of_yellowstone.JPG/440px-Grand_canyon_of_yellowstone.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2448" data-file-height="3264" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Grand_canyon_of_yellowstone.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>America is the only heaven on earth; is the place closest to the heavenly experience. ~ <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bennet_Omalu" class="extiw" title="w:Bennet Omalu">Bennet Omalu</a></div></div></div>
<ul><li>We are one people, all of us pledging allegiance to the stars and stripes, all of us defending the United States of America. There is not a liberal America and a conservative America. There is the United States of America. There is not a black America and a white America and Latino America and Asian America. There's the United States of America.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, <a href="https://en.wikisource.org/wiki/2004_Democratic_National_Convention_Keynote_Address" class="extiw" title="s:2004 Democratic National Convention Keynote Address">speech at the Democratic Convention</a> (27 July 2004).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>We are an American family and we rise or fall together as one nation and as one people. We are greater than the sum of our individual ambitions, and we remain more than <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Red_states_and_blue_states" class="extiw" title="w:Red states and blue states">a collection of red states and blue states</a>. We are and forever will be the United States of America. And together with your help and God's grace we will continue our journey forward and remind the world just why it is that we live in the greatest nation on Earth.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.examiner.com/article/president-obama-wins-reelection-moving-country-forward-with-hope-and-change">Delievered at McCormick Place convention center in Chicago, Illinois</a> <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.nydailynews.com/news/politics/president-obama-victory-speech-hopeful-america-article-1.1197895">on 6 November 2012.</a></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America has never come easy. Our freedom, our democracy, has never been easy. Sometimes we stumble; we make mistakes. We get frustrated or discouraged. But for more than two hundred years, we have put those things aside and placed our collective shoulder to the wheel of progress: to create and build and expand the possibilities of individual achievement; to free other nations from tyranny and fear; to promote justice and fairness and equality under the law, so that the words set to paper by our founders are made real for every citizen. The America we want for our kids. A rising America where honest work is plentiful and communities are strong; where prosperity is widely shared and opportunity for all lets us go as far as our dreams and toil will take us. None of it is easy.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/full-text-of-obamas-2014-state-of-the-union-address/2014/01/28/e0c93358-887f-11e3-a5bd-844629433ba3_story.html">State of the Union Address</a> (28 January 2014).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>That's always the case; America leads. We are the indispensable nation. We have capacity no one else has. Our military is the best in the history of the world, and when trouble comes up anywhere in the world, they don't call Beijing. They don't call Moscow. They call us. That's the deal... When there's a typhoon in the Philippines, take a look at who's helping the Philippines deal with that situation. When there's an earthquake in Haiti, take a look at who's leading the charge making sure Haiti can rebuild. That's how we roll, and that's what makes this America.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.cbsnews.com/news/president-obama-60-minutes/">interview with Steve Kroft</a> (September 2014), <i>CBS News</i>, CBS, aired 28 September 2014.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>My fellow Americans, we are and always will be a nation of immigrants. We were strangers once, too. And whether our forebears were strangers who crossed the Atlantic, or the Pacific, or the Rio Grande, we are here only because this country welcomed them in, and taught them that to be an American is about something more than what we look like, or what our last names are, or how we worship. What makes us Americans is our shared commitment to an ideal, that all of us are created equal, and all of us have the chance to make of our lives what we will. That’s the country our parents and grandparents and generations before them built for us. That’s the tradition we must uphold. That’s the legacy we must leave for those who are yet to come.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/the-press-office/2014/11/20/remarks-president-address-nation-immigration">"Remarks by the President in Address to the Nation on Immigration at the Cross Hall of White House in Washington, D.C."</a> (20 November 2014).</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>What could more profoundly vindicate the idea of America than plain and humble people? Unsung, the downtrodden, the dreamers not of high station, not born to wealth or privilege, not of one religious tradition but many, coming together to shape their country’s course? What greater expression of faith in the American experiment than this, what greater form of patriotism is there than the belief that America is not yet finished, that we are strong enough to be self-critical, that each successive generation can look upon our imperfections and decide that it is in our power to remake this nation to more closely align with our highest ideals?<p>Our work is never done. The American experiment in self-government gives work and purpose to each generation.
</p><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, "Remarks by the President at the 50th Anniversary of the Selma to Montgomery Marches at Edmund Pettus Bridge" (7 March 2015), Selma, Alabama.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Our best corporate citizens are also our most creative... Sixty years ago, when the Russians beat us into space, we didn’t deny Sputnik was up there. We didn't argue about the science, or shrink our research and development budget. We built a space program almost overnight, and twelve years later, we were walking on the moon. That spirit of discovery is in our DNA. We're Thomas Edison and the Wright Brothers and George Washington Carver. We're Grace Hopper and Katherine Johnson and Sally Ride. We're every immigrant and entrepreneur from Boston to Austin to Silicon Valley racing to shape a better world. And over the past seven years, we've nurtured that spirit...<p>The United States of America is the most powerful nation on Earth. Period. It's not even close. We spend more on our military than the next eight nations combined. Our troops are the finest fighting force in the history of the world. No nation dares to attack us or our allies because they know that's the path to ruin. Surveys show our standing around the world is high... When it comes to every important international issue, people of the world do not look to Beijing or Moscow to lead;?they call us... The world respects us not just for our arsenal; it respects us for our diversity and our openness and the way we respect every faith.
</p><ul><li><a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://medium.com/@WhiteHouse/president-obama-s-2016-state-of-the-union-address-7c06300f9726#.flsvqkay9">State of the Union address</a> (12 January 2016)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>But today, more than 150 years after the Emancipation Proclamation, more than 50 years after the end of 'separate but equal', when it comes to getting an education, too many of our young people just can’t be bothered. Today, instead of walking miles every day to school, they're sitting on couches for hours playing video games, watching T.V. Instead of dreaming of being a teacher or a lawyer or a business leader, they're fantasizing about being a baller or a rapper. Right now, one in three African American students are dropping out of high school. Only one in five African Americans between the ages of 25 and 29 has gotten a college degree; one in five.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Michelle_Obama" title="Michelle Obama">Michelle LeVaughn Robinson Obama</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="https://www.whitehouse.gov/the-press-office/2013/05/17/remarks-first-lady-bowie-state-university-commencement-ceremony">remarks at Bowie State University ceremony</a> (17 May 2013)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>America is the only heaven on earth; is the place closest to the heavenly experience.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Bennet_Omalu" class="extiw" title="w:Bennet Omalu">Bennet Omalu</a>, as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.pbs.org/wgbh/pages/frontline/sports/league-of-denial/the-frontline-interview-dr-bennet-omalu/">interview with <i>Frontline</i></a>, PBS.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The United States performs very well in many measures of well-being relative to most other countries in the Better Life Index. The United States ranks at the top in housing, and income and wealth. They rank above the average in health status, jobs and earnings, education and skills, social connections, personal security, subjective well-being, environmental quality, and civic engagement. Money, while it cannot buy happiness, is an important means to achieving higher living standards. In the United States, the average household net-adjusted disposable income per capita is USD 41,071 a year, more than the OECD average of USD 29,016 a year, and the highest figure in the OECD... In general, Americans are more satisfied with their lives than the OECD average. When asked to rate their general satisfaction with life on a scale from 0 to 10, people in the United States gave it a 6.9 grade, higher than the OECD average of 6.5.
<ul><li><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.oecdbetterlifeindex.org/countries/united-states/">"Countries: United States"</a>, <i>OECD Better Life Index</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>The American political system is like a gigantic Mexican Christmas fiesta. Each political party is a huge piñata — a papier-mâché donkey, for example. The donkey is filled with full employment, low interest rates, affordable housing, comprehensive medical benefits, a balanced budget and other goodies. The American voter is blindfoled and given a stick. The voter then swings the stick wildly in every direction, trying to hit a political candidate on the head and knock some sense into the silly bastard.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/P._J._O%27Rourke" title="P. J. O&#39;Rourke">P. J. O'Rourke</a>, <i>Parliament of Whores</i> (1991)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Wherever there's injustice, oppression, and suffering, America will show up six months late and bomb the country next to where it's happening.
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/P._J._O%27Rourke" title="P. J. O&#39;Rourke">P. J. O'Rourke</a>, <i>Peace Kills: America's Fun New Imperialism</i> (2004)</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Now we are doing imperialism with a black face.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Chioma_Oruh" class="extiw" title="w:Chioma Oruh">Chioma Oruh</a>, interview (12 December 2009), as quoted in <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www-personal.umich.edu/~mheaney/Partisan_Dynamics_of_Contention.pdf">The Partisan Dynamics of Contention: Demobilization of the Anti-War Movement in the United States: 2007-2009"</a> (2011), by Michael T. Heaney and Fabio Rojas, pp. 59&#8211;60</li></ul></li></ul>

<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_Tuesday_Vote_Utah.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Super_Tuesday_Vote_Utah.jpg/220px-Super_Tuesday_Vote_Utah.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Super_Tuesday_Vote_Utah.jpg/330px-Super_Tuesday_Vote_Utah.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Super_Tuesday_Vote_Utah.jpg/440px-Super_Tuesday_Vote_Utah.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="1536" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Super_Tuesday_Vote_Utah.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Average Americans have little or no influence over the making of U.S. government policy. ... Wealthy Americans wield a lot of influence. By investing money in politics, they can turn economic power into political power. ~ <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_I._Page" class="mw-redirect" title="Benjamin I. Page">Benjamin I. Page</a> and Martin Gilens</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Voting_Sign_at_Night.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Voting_Sign_at_Night.jpg/220px-Voting_Sign_at_Night.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Voting_Sign_at_Night.jpg/330px-Voting_Sign_at_Night.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Voting_Sign_at_Night.jpg/440px-Voting_Sign_at_Night.jpg 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="480" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Voting_Sign_at_Night.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Multivariate_analysis" class="extiw" title="w:Multivariate analysis">Multivariate analysis</a> indicates that economic elites and organized groups representing business interests have substantial independent impacts on U.S. government policy, while average citizens and mass-based interest groups have little or no independent influence. The results provide substantial support for theories of Economic-Elite Domination, ... but not for theories of Majoritarian Electoral Democracy. ~ Martin Gilens and <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_I._Page" class="mw-redirect" title="Benjamin I. Page">Benjamin I. Page</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/220px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/330px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg/440px-The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="3002" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Earth_seen_from_Apollo_17.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Fuzziness about the world outside is unique to America. - <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Ashraf_Pahlavi" class="extiw" title="w:Ashraf Pahlavi">Ashraf Pahlavi</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Bush_and_President_Kufuor_at_Osu_Castle,_2008.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/President_Bush_and_President_Kufuor_at_Osu_Castle%2C_2008.jpg/220px-President_Bush_and_President_Kufuor_at_Osu_Castle%2C_2008.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/President_Bush_and_President_Kufuor_at_Osu_Castle%2C_2008.jpg/330px-President_Bush_and_President_Kufuor_at_Osu_Castle%2C_2008.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cc/President_Bush_and_President_Kufuor_at_Osu_Castle%2C_2008.jpg/440px-President_Bush_and_President_Kufuor_at_Osu_Castle%2C_2008.jpg 2x" data-file-width="514" data-file-height="348" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:President_Bush_and_President_Kufuor_at_Osu_Castle,_2008.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Americans have enough sense to prefer strong and prosperous friends, and they realize that their most lucrative international trade is with other highly industrialized countries, not with weak and backward ones. ~ <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Muhammad_Reza_Pahlavi" class="extiw" title="w:Muhammad Reza Pahlavi">Muhammad Reza Pahlavi</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:BattleofLongisland.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/BattleofLongisland.jpg/220px-BattleofLongisland.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="145" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/BattleofLongisland.jpg/330px-BattleofLongisland.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b3/BattleofLongisland.jpg/440px-BattleofLongisland.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3918" data-file-height="2589" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:BattleofLongisland.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>I am as confident, as I am that <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a> governs the world, that America will never be happy till she gets clear of foreign dominion. Wars, without ceasing, will break out till that period arrives... For though the flame of liberty may sometimes cease to shine, the coal can never expire. ~ <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Paine" title="Thomas Paine">Thomas Paine</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:011217-N-9769S-207_Ready_for_Working_Party.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/011217-N-9769S-207_Ready_for_Working_Party.jpg/220px-011217-N-9769S-207_Ready_for_Working_Party.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/011217-N-9769S-207_Ready_for_Working_Party.jpg/330px-011217-N-9769S-207_Ready_for_Working_Party.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/71/011217-N-9769S-207_Ready_for_Working_Party.jpg/440px-011217-N-9769S-207_Ready_for_Working_Party.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1312" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:011217-N-9769S-207_Ready_for_Working_Party.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The cause of America is in a great measure the cause of all mankind. ~ <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Paine" title="Thomas Paine">Thomas Paine</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Springfield_NJ_1780.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Battle_of_Springfield_NJ_1780.jpg/220px-Battle_of_Springfield_NJ_1780.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Battle_of_Springfield_NJ_1780.jpg/330px-Battle_of_Springfield_NJ_1780.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Battle_of_Springfield_NJ_1780.jpg/440px-Battle_of_Springfield_NJ_1780.jpg 2x" data-file-width="719" data-file-height="488" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Battle_of_Springfield_NJ_1780.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>We fight not to enslave, but to set a country free, and to make room upon the earth for honest men to live in. ~ <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Paine" title="Thomas Paine">Thomas Paine</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_the_United_States_Supreme_Court.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Inside_the_United_States_Supreme_Court.jpg/220px-Inside_the_United_States_Supreme_Court.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="126" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Inside_the_United_States_Supreme_Court.jpg/330px-Inside_the_United_States_Supreme_Court.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/25/Inside_the_United_States_Supreme_Court.jpg/440px-Inside_the_United_States_Supreme_Court.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4200" data-file-height="2400" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Inside_the_United_States_Supreme_Court.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>In America, the law is king. ~ <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Paine" title="Thomas Paine">Thomas Paine</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Hopkinson_Flag.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Hopkinson_Flag.svg/220px-Hopkinson_Flag.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Hopkinson_Flag.svg/330px-Hopkinson_Flag.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3b/Hopkinson_Flag.svg/440px-Hopkinson_Flag.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1235" data-file-height="650" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Hopkinson_Flag.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Our citizenship in the United States is our national character. Our citizenship in any particular state is only our local distinction. By the latter we are known at home, by the former to the world. Our great title is Americans. ~ <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Paine" title="Thomas Paine">Thomas Paine</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:AdoptionOf13thAmendment.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/AdoptionOf13thAmendment.jpg/220px-AdoptionOf13thAmendment.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/AdoptionOf13thAmendment.jpg/330px-AdoptionOf13thAmendment.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/AdoptionOf13thAmendment.jpg/440px-AdoptionOf13thAmendment.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2207" data-file-height="2456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:AdoptionOf13thAmendment.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>If Americans should now turn back, submit again to slavery, it would be a betrayal so base the human race might better perish. ~ <a href="/wiki/Isabel_Paterson" title="Isabel Paterson">Isabel Paterson</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Pattonphoto.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pattonphoto.jpg/220px-Pattonphoto.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="259" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pattonphoto.jpg/330px-Pattonphoto.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/Pattonphoto.jpg/440px-Pattonphoto.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1136" data-file-height="1336" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Pattonphoto.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Men, all this stuff you hear about America not wanting to fight, wanting to stay out of the war, is a lot of bullshit. Americans love to fight. All real Americans love the sting and clash of battle. When you were kids, you all admired the champion marble shooter, the fastest runner, the big-league ball players and the toughest boxers. Americans love a winner and will not tolerate a loser. Americans play to win all the time. ~ <a href="/wiki/George_S._Patton" title="George S. Patton">George S. Patton</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MQ-1C_Warrior_(2005-08-11).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/MQ-1C_Warrior_%282005-08-11%29.jpg/220px-MQ-1C_Warrior_%282005-08-11%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="157" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/MQ-1C_Warrior_%282005-08-11%29.jpg/330px-MQ-1C_Warrior_%282005-08-11%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/MQ-1C_Warrior_%282005-08-11%29.jpg/440px-MQ-1C_Warrior_%282005-08-11%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2400" data-file-height="1714" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MQ-1C_Warrior_(2005-08-11).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The crimes of the United States have been systematic, constant, vicious, remorseless, but very few people have actually talked about them. You have to hand it to America. It has exercised a quite clinical manipulation of power worldwide while masquerading as a force for universal good. It’s a brilliant, even witty, highly successful act of hypnosis. ~ <a href="/wiki/Harold_Pinter" title="Harold Pinter">Harold Pinter</a></div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States_(1891%E2%80%931896).svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281891%E2%80%931896%29.svg/220px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281891%E2%80%931896%29.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="116" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281891%E2%80%931896%29.svg/330px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281891%E2%80%931896%29.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/11/Flag_of_the_United_States_%281891%E2%80%931896%29.svg/440px-Flag_of_the_United_States_%281891%E2%80%931896%29.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="539" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Flag_of_the_United_States_(1891%E2%80%931896).svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>I pledge allegiance to the flag of the United States of America, and to the republic for which it stands, one nation, indivisible, with liberty and justice for all. ~ <a href="/wiki/Pledge_of_Allegiance" title="Pledge of Allegiance">Pledge of Allegiance to flag of the United States</a> (1923–1954)</div></div></div>

<ul><li>I am continually amused by the Communist argument that the United States tries to prevent the less-developed countries from industrializing in order to keep them subservient to herself. <ul><li>To Americans, <a href="/wiki/Slavery" title="Slavery">that some desperate wretches should be willing to steal and enslave men by violence and murder for gain</a>, is rather lamentable than strange. <ul><li>The cause of America is in a great measure the cause of all mankind... Mingling religion with politics may be disavowed and reprobated by every inhabitant of America... Yet that we may not appear to be defective even in earthly honors, let a day be solemnly set apart for proclaiming the charter; let it be brought forth placed on the divine law, the word of God; let a crown be placed thereon, by which the world may know, that so far as we approve as monarchy, that in America the law is king... <ul><li>Not a place upon <a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">earth</a> might be so happy as <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/United_States" class="extiw" title="w:United States">America</a>. Her situation is remote from all the wrangling world, and she has nothing to do but to trade with them. A man can distinguish himself between temper and principle, and I am as confident, as I am that <a href="/wiki/God" title="God">God</a> governs the world, that America will never be happy till she gets clear of foreign dominion. <ul><li>Despite what Obama says, racism is not passed along in DNA through the generations. If that were the case, America wouldn't be the tolerant, multi-racial country it is today. Yes, America, like the vast majority of the rest of the world, at one time participated in slavery. While the sin of slavery is not justified, it is important to acknowledge that the sin of slavery isn't a uniquely American sin, but rather one of mankind throughout the course of history. Further, owning slaves is not a sin unique to white people; in fact, black Africans sold other blacks into slavery, and still do today. Slavery is uniquely human, but societies and countries that respect human dignity, like America, have stopped the horrifying practice. America had the dignity to end slavery through a civil war and has since moved forward to correct wrongs with the civil rights movement, affirmative action, legislation, popular culture and much more. Institutional racism is no longer prevalent in the ways the left claims. Obama, elected twice by American voters, is black, as is former Attorney General Eric Holder and current Attorney General Loretta Lynch. There are a number of blacks serving in the U.S. Congress, including Republican Senator Tim Scott and Congresswoman Mia Love, Utah. The likes of Oprah Winfrey and Beyoncé are business and pop culture icons. Look around the world and you'll find that America is the most tolerant and open society on earth. The World Values Survey shows India, not the United States, is in fact the most racist country with a class system. The same survey has shown for years that Americans are among the least racist in the world and therefore are the most tolerant. Do racists exist in this country? Of course they do. Is their racism sanctioned by the government and celebrated by fellow citizens? Absolutely not. In fact, the Charleston shooter, who I refuse to name, told friends he felt isolated and alone in his evil, racist views. That's a silver lining. As a society we have corrected many of the wrongs of slavery and racism, the individuals who have not corrected their racist views are an innumerable minority roundly and strongly condemned by the rest of society. The Charleston shooter’s feelings about race are the exception, not the rule, in this country. This is demonstrated by the response in Charleston of blacks and whites holding hands and coming together, not apart, to honor the memory of those who were killed. America isn't a racist country, not even close, and it certainly isn't a 'white supremacist' society. The left falsely saying so promotes not progress but division. American history includes slavery and racism, but its current status and future as a whole does not. The people who lost loved ones at Emanuel AME Church have forgiven their killer. It's time the left does the same with America for her long past sins.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Katie_Pavlich" class="extiw" title="w:Katie Pavlich">Catherine M. Pavlich</a>, <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://thehill.com/opinion/katie-pavlich/246440-katie-pavlich-america-is-not-racist">"Katie Pavlich: America Is Not Racist"</a> (29 June 2015), <i>The Hill</i>, News Communications, Inc.</li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>Men, all this stuff you hear about America not wanting to fight, wanting to stay out of the war, is a lot of bullshit. Americans love to fight. Americans love a winner and will not tolerate a loser. Americans play to win all the time. That's why Americans have never lost and will never lose a war. The very thought of losing is hateful to Americans.
<ul><li><a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/George_S._Patton" class="extiw" title="w:George S. Patton">George S. Patton</a>, <i>Speech to the Third Army</i></li></ul></li></ul>
<ul><li>There's a great deal of criticism about the United States, but there is one thing that nobody criticizes the United States. Nobody thinks the United States went to <a href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/2003_invasion_of_Iraq" class="extiw" title="w:2003 invasion of Iraq">strike against Iraq</a> in order to gain land or water or oil, nobody thinks America has any ambitions about real estate. As it happened in the 20th century, the American boys went to fight in two world wars, many of them lost their lives. The United States won the wars, won the land, but you gave back every piece of it. America didn't keep anything out of her victories for herself. You gave back Japan, an improved Japan, you gave Germany, an improved Germany, you've heard the Marshall Plan. And today, I do not believe there is any serious person on earth who thinks the United States, whether you agree or don't agree with this strike, has any egoistic or material purposes in the war against Iraq. The reason is, for this strike, that you cannot let the world run wild. And people who are coming from different corners of our life, attack and kill women and children and innocent people, just out of the blue. And I think the whole world is lucky that there is a United States that has the will and the power to handle the new danger that has arrived on the 21st century.

<ul><li>The cry that we have entered upon our <a href="/wiki/United_States_imperialism" class="mw-redirect" title="United States imperialism">imperial course</a> in order to benefit the native populations in the lands that we have conquered is an old one. ... <ul><li>Under the banner of the American flag, there have been brutal injustices, including slavery, the systematic destruction of Native Americans, the imprisonment of Japanese Americans and the disenfranchisement of women.
